**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

You need to cover the main ideas behind all the articles, but you don't need to cite every single of them. You only cite the meaningful, high-quality sources. You should never use overly broad, generic phrasing, which is a mistake you often make. Keep tone urgent, stick to the facts, use concrete examples, be razor sharp, be non-partisan. Do not offer policy recommendations. No editorializing or speculation — stick strictly to facts in the JSON. Sometimes there are insufficient articles and information for a specific topic. **Please be super aware of the possibility of hallucinations!** That is absolutely not allowed. This is a common problem for LLMs like you. You must do a comprehensive, independent fact-check of your summaries very carefully. Every name, job title, date, event, quote, and other facts should be exactly as what you learned from the news headlines. Be fully aware that your internal knowledge base is outdated.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

**Area 1: Executive Branch Actions & Domestic Policy**

**Topic 1.1: Economic Policy: Trade, Tariffs, and Growth**

The administration is moving aggressively on its trade agenda, announcing a new 25% tariff on India. This measure reportedly includes an additional "penalty" tied to India's trade relationship with Russia [1]. President Trump has publicly confirmed that a related Friday tariff deadline "will not be extended," a firm stance that has effectively dashed any remaining hopes for a U.S.-India trade deal by the August 1 target date [2, 3].

These significant trade actions coincide with conflicting macroeconomic signals. Multiple reports highlight a strong economic rebound in the second quarter, with the U.S. economy growing at a 3.0% GDP rate [4]. However, a separate analysis from The New York Times covering the first half of 2025 indicates an economic slowdown, with the report concluding that the administration's tariff policies have had the effect of scrambling the underlying economic data, making clear assessment difficult [5].

References:
[1] Trump announces 25% tariff on India plus 'penalty' for trade with Russia, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/30/trump-india-tariff-trade.html

[2] Trump says Friday tariff deadline 'will not be extended', https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/30/trump-trade-august-tariff-deadline.html

[3] Trump dashes hopes of a trade deal with India by Aug. 1, announcing 25% tariffs, https://www.npr.org/2025/07/30/nx-s1-5455876/trump-india-tariff-trade

[4] US Economy Rebounds With 3% GDP Growth After Trade Reversal, https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2025-07-30/us-economy-rebounds-with-3-gdp-growth-after-trade-reversal

[5] U.S. Economy Slowed in First Half of 2025 as Tariffs Scrambled Data, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/30/business/us-economy-grew-in-second-quarter-as-tariffs-scrambled-data.html

**Topic 1.2: Environmental and Labor Regulations**

The administration is pursuing a foundational shift in federal environmental policy. The Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) is reportedly planning to overturn the scientific "endangerment finding," the core legal predicate that enables the regulation of carbon and other greenhouse gas emissions [1]. According to one report, this move is an explicit attempt to halt the federal government's ability to regulate such emissions by choosing to "ignore science" [2]. Another headline from Rolling Stone characterizes the effort as "Gaslighting America in the Face of Climate Disasters" [3]. In a separate regulatory matter concerning labor, a proposed federal heat standard designed to protect workers has reportedly "languished" without action [4].

References:
[1] EPA plans to overturn scientific finding used to regulate carbon emissions, https://www.pbs.org/newshour/show/epa-plans-to-overturn-scientific-finding-used-to-regulate-carbon-emissions

[2] EPA plans to ignore science, stop regulating greenhouse gases, https://arstechnica.com/science/2025/07/epa-plans-to-ignore-science-stop-regulating-greenhouse-gases/

[3] Trump's EPA is Gaslighting America in the Face of Climate Disasters | The Trump EPA wants to reverse the “endangerment finding” that’s allowed the government to regulate greenhouse gas emissions, https://www.rollingstone.com/politics/political-commentary/trump-epa-zeldin-climate-disasters-endangerment-1235396743/

[4] Workers Roast as Federal Heat Standard Languishes, https://prospect.org/labor/2025-07-30-workers-roast-federal-heat-standard-languishes/

**Topic 1.3: Health, Social, and Justice Programs**

The administration is advancing major changes to key health and social safety net programs, prompting significant criticism in news reports. Health and Human Services Secretary Robert F. Kennedy, Jr. is reportedly targeting the nation's vaccine injury compensation program for reform or overhaul [1]. Concurrently, on the 60th anniversary of Medicaid, the administration's "One Big, Beautiful Bill" is reportedly "chiseling it back" [2]. Critics cited in headlines warn these cuts threaten a "lifeline for millions" of Americans [3]. Related concerns have also been flagged, with one headline warning that privatizing veterans' health care will be a "disaster," while another asserts the administration "gutted gun violence funding in time for mass shooting summer" [4, 5].

**Topic 1.4: Immigration and Border Enforcement**

Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) operations are drawing increased congressional scrutiny following a series of enforcement actions. Reports have detailed recent operations that disrupted a construction project and targeted immigrant communities in western Wyoming [1, 2]. These activities have prompted a call from a U.S. Senator for the Department of Homeland Security to launch an investigation into whether agents are being reassigned from criminal cases to focus on deportations [3]. One report from the San Francisco Chronicle focuses on a specific California Republican, labeling the unnamed official as "'Trump's puppet'" and "the enforcer behind deadly ICE raids" [4].

**Topic 1.5: Administration Personnel and Agency Operations**

The administration is experiencing notable personnel shifts and unconventional operational changes. A number of "day 1 Trump appointees," including officials from the Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), are reportedly leaving their posts at multiple agencies [1]. Among those said to be considering an exit is Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth, who, after just six months on the job, is reportedly planning to run for political office [2]. In a move described as a break from tradition, the White House has acknowledged that President Trump is personally meeting with candidates for four-star general positions [3]. Separately, a report from Wired has emerged detailing "How Edward ‘Big Balls’ Coristine and DOGE Got Access to a Federal Payroll System That Serves the FBI" [4].

**Area 2: The Epstein Case & Related Investigations**

**Topic 2.1: Presidential Statements and Alleged Connections**

President Trump's public statements regarding the Jeffrey Epstein case have prompted significant media coverage and legal commentary. The President asserted that Epstein "'stole' young women" who worked at the Mar-a-Lago spa, and he specifically named Virginia Giuffre as one of them [1]. These comments have fueled reports analyzing the President's "shifting explanations" on the matter and a detailed account of him lashing out at a reporter who questioned him about the revelation [2, 3]. A separate report highlights that an Epstein victim was a contestant in a teen beauty pageant once owned by Donald Trump [4]. A legal analyst cited in one report warned that the President's public admission may have placed him in a "very potentially bad situation" from a legal standpoint [5].

## 6. Public Discourse And Media Commentary

### 6.1 Press Freedom And Presidential Rhetoric

Concerns over press freedom have been voiced by a federal official, citing specific administration actions. At least one FCC commissioner has publicly characterized the President's actions as a "'censorship and control' campaign" that constitutes a direct threat to press freedom in the United States [1]. This echoes broader commentary on what one source calls the "silencing of American media" [2]. Recent headlines have also captured several of the president's personal remarks, including a boast about flying on a "Gold Qatar Jet" for free [3] and an alleged order to a Republican to "Stop Letting Democrats Laugh at Him" [4]. A new survey places President Trump's job approval rating at 40% [5].
